+Jamison Brereton

164
All Gods (Riddle Hymn)
D─лrghatamas Aucathya
52 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 12, 15, 23, 29, 36, 41; prast─Бrapaс╣Еkti 42; anuс╣гс╣нubh 51
The Anukramaс╣З─л assigns this hymn to a variety of gods: All the Gods (1тАУ41), Speech (42a, 45), the Waters (42b), Dung-smoke (43a), Soma (43b), Agni, S┼лrya, V─Бyu (44), S┼лrya (46, 47), the Wheel of the Seasons (48), Sarasvat─л (49), the S─Бdhyas (50), S┼лrya or Parjanya or Agni (51), Sarasvant or S┼лrya (52). Such diversity creates the impression that this hymn is a fairly loose assemblage, although its thematic and structural programs indicate that the hymn, or the bulk of it, constitutes a coherent composition. Among the more recent and significant studies of the hymn are those of Brown (1968) and Houben (2000), which also discuss older interpretations and upon which we have drawn extensively and gratefully.
The hymn has continued to attract scholarly attention in part because it has continued to escape satisfying interpretation. One reason is that the hymn was com posed to be enigmatic, to be never fully decipherable. But even if we will never be able to solve all its puzzles, we can appreciate how it functions as an enigma and perhaps why. Since the hymn makes both implicit and explicit reference to Vedic rit ual, including rites other than the soma ritual, one way into the hymn is through its connections to ritual. Even though the later ritual application of R╠еgvedic hymns is not always a reliable guide to their original ritual contexts, it offers a place to start. According to Aitareya ─Аraс╣Зyaka V.3.2, verses 1тАУ41 are part of the Vai┼Ыvadeva┼Ыastra, a recitation at the midday offerings of the Mah─Бvrata ceremony, and ┼Ъ─Бс╣Еkh─Бyana ─Аraс╣Зyaka II.18 places the whole of the hymn in the Mah─Бvrata rite. This Mah─Бvrata rite is a variation of the Agniс╣гс╣нoma soma ritual that was performed on the next to last day of the year-long Gav─Бmayana rite. It may well be that the application of the hymn in the Mah─Бvrata rite is secondary (Houben 2000: 502), since there is no explicit reference to the Mah─Бvrata in the hymn and, for such a long hymn, little even to the soma sacrifice more generally. But there is a thematic connection between this hymn and the Mah─Бvrata. According to Kauс╣г─лtak─л Br─Бhmaс╣Зa XIX.3, the Mah─Бvrata fell on the winter solstice. Whatever else I.164 may be about, much of it concerns the sun in one way or another (e.g., vss. 2, 7, 8, 10, 11, 14, 25, 33, 44, 46, 48). The winter solstice, when the sun has halted its southward movement and is about to turn northward, would be a natural time to consider the sun and its appearance and therefore may provide the seasonal context for the hymn.
A second ritual context for the hymn is the Pravargya rite, which is an offering of heated milk and ghee to the A┼Ыvins. In the classical Agniс╣гс╣нoma soma ritual, the Pravargya was performed twice daily on the three days leading up the soma-pressing day; originally, however, it may have been a rite independent of the soma ritual. The ┼Ыrautas┼лtras (cf. van Buitenen 1968: 93, 96тАУ98) prescribe the recitation of verses 26тАУ28, 31 (=X.177.3), and 49 in the Pravargya, and at least verses 26тАУ29 refer

directly to the Pravargya rite. Thus, as Houben (2000) has demonstrated, significant parts of this hymn are concerned with the Pravargya.
These two rituals, the Mah─Бvrata and the Pravargya, have one thing in com mon: they are the principal subjects of ─Аraс╣Зyaka texts. The ─Аraс╣Зyakas or тАЬfor estтАЭ books are later Vedic works that explored rituals and the interpretations of rituals thought to be too dangerous to be taught within the village. The R╠еgvedic ─Аraс╣Зyakas concern especially the Mah─Бvrata rite, and the Yajurvedic ─Аraс╣Зyakas, the Pravargya. In our view this hymn was not primarily composed for recitation in a particular rite, although to be sure some of its mantras were ritually employed. Rather, this poem is an early example of ─Аraс╣Зyaka-like interpretation. Its function is to disclose the meaning of the rites, particularly the Mah─Бvrata and Pravargya rites. It might seem odd that a R╠еgvedic hymn could anticipate the later ─Аraс╣Зyaka literature. However, according to the ┼Ъ─Бс╣Еkh─Бyana Gс╣Ыhya S┼лtra II.11.13, once a stu dent has learned the saс╣Гhit─Б, his teacher may guide him though the rahasya, the secret teaching, which the s┼лtra defines as the ─Аraс╣Зyaka (cf. Oldenberg 1888: 291). Even if, as Oldenberg (293) argues, study of the rahasya meant the recitation of the mantras of the Mah─Бvrata, not study of the interpretation of the rite, the s┼лtra still points toward a direct pathway between the R╠еgveda and the study that eventually came to constitute the R╠еgvedic ─Аraс╣Зyakas.
Key to grasping the meaning of the ritual is understanding the links between ritual acts and both the cosmos and the person. The complexity of the hymn derives especially from the multiplicity of reference of its verses, which connect ritual, cosmos, and person. Thus, the verses frequently refer simultaneously to the ritual (adhiyaj├▒am) and to the world (adhidevatam), especially to the sun, and sometimes also to the human body or the human being (adhy─Бtmam). There is no unproblematic verse in this hymn, but as an example, consider the possibilities of the first verse. Lines abc of that verse describe three brothers: the gray Hotar, the ravenous middle brother, and the brother with ghee-smeared back. Scholars have offered a variety of identifications for the brothers: the sun, wind, and fire (S─Бyaс╣Зa); the ─Аhavan─лya or offering fire, the Dakс╣гiс╣Зa or southern fire, and the G─Бrhapatya or household fire (Geldner); the original form of Agni, lightning, and the terres trial Agni (Brown); and the sun, lightning, and the fire heating the Pravargya pot (Houben). It is likely that ancient hearers of the hymn made not one but several of these sets of identifications. In our view the verse has both a ritual (adhiyaj├▒am) and a cosmic (adhidevatam) meaning. On the one hand, the three brothers can be a triad of ritual firesтАФeither the three that Geldner sees or perhaps three phases of the sacrificial fire (gray embers, flaming fire, and fire flaring as it receives ghee). But they can also be a triad of cosmic fires (perhaps the sun, moon, and earthly fire, which correspond to the three ritual fires, or another of the identifications proposed above). In 1d the clanlord and his seven sons refer primarily to the sacrificer and the seven priests (cf. II.1.2). But the sacrificer might also be embodied in the Sun and the seven priests in Agni, or the clanlord might be the Sun and his seven sons, the stars of the constellation of the Seven Seers, Ursa Major. We will never know which of these or what other interpretations the poet intended, but it is likely that the verse operates on several levels that connect ritual and cosmos.
The brief exegetical possibilities we have provided in the translation at best sug gest primary referents, even though other secondary identifications may also be implied. So, for example, verses 2 and 3 move back and forth between adhiyaj├▒am and adhidevatam meanings. The тАЬsevenтАЭ in 2a appear to be the тАЬsevenтАЭ of 1d, who are primarily priests (an adhiyaj├▒am interpretation). However, the тАЬsingle wheelтАЭ in 2a suggests the sun (adhidevatam) more than the ritual fire. This interpretation is supported by verse 48, since there the single wheel is the disk of the sun, which is drawn by the тАЬsingle horse,тАЭ Eta┼Ыa, the horse that pulls the SunтАЩs chariot. In verse 3 the poet foregrounds ritual referents: the seven may again be priests, and, as is often the case, the chariot has now become a symbol of the sacrifice itself.
Another characteristic of this hymn, and another reason for its obscurity, is its fre quent use of word play. The poet favors words that are not etymologically or semanti cally related but that sound as if they ought to be. For example, in verse 13d san─Б╠Бd тАЬfrom of oldтАЭ is echoed by sa╠Бn─Бbhiс╕е тАЬalong with its naveтАЭ and in 14a sa╠Бnemi тАЬalong
with its felly.тАЭ Or again, in 14a v├н v─Бvr╠еta тАЬhas turned awayтАЭ anticipates 14c ─Б╠Бvr╠еtam тАЬcovered over.тАЭ In verse 5 aja╠Б тАЬunbornтАЭ can also mean тАЬgoat,тАЭ and therefore can sug gest Aja Ekapad, the тАЬOne-Footed Goat,тАЭ a symbol of the Sun. According to Thieme (1987: 338), the poet even uses an implied homophone in verse 16. The stars of the constellation called тАЬthe Kr╠еttik─БsтАЭ are envisioned as women. The word for тАЬwomenтАЭ in p─Бda a is str├нyaс╕е from the stem str─л╠Б. There is also a closely homophonous mascu line stem st┼Х╠е тАЬstar,тАЭ which does not occur in the verse but which would have been known to its hearers. The poet is saying that although the Kr╠еttik─Бs are str─л╠Б тАЬwomen,тАЭ people call its constituents st┼Х╠е тАЬstars,тАЭ and therefore they speak of those Kr╠еttik─Бs, even though they are women, as masculine тАЬstars.тАЭ As the verse concludes, only a poet who a master of words would understand this, and a poet who does understand
it becomes even greater than his father, who would likely have been his teacher. Thematic continuities and repeated use of similar poetic devices help unify the hymn. The hymn is also unified by its recursive structure created by parallelisms in its beginning and conclusion. For example, the poet speaks of the One (e╠Бka) in verse 6 and again toward the end of the hymn, in verse 46. In verse 6 that which is the тАЬOneтАЭ assumes the form of the Sun. At the other end of the poem, in verse 46, the One reappears and, through speech, takes the form not only of the Sun, but also of Agni, of M─Бtari┼Ыvan (the fire-bringer), and of other deities as well. Verses 7cd and 47 (as well as verse 51) describe the course of the waters upward by means of the rays of the sun and then downward as rain. Verses 2тАУ3 and verse 48 describe the SunтАЩs chariot and especially its single wheel. The final verses, 49тАУ52, form an independent recursive unit. Verses 49 and 52 concern respectively the femi nine Sarasvat─л, the river goddess, and the masculine Sarasvant, who is Agni and the Sun according to 52ab. The linkage of fire and water or sun and rain is a constant throughout the hymn. It is reasserted in the verses fitted between those to Sarasvat─л and Sarasvant. Verse 51 describes the cycle of the water to heaven and then back

down to earth and the correspondence between the sacrificial fire that invigorates the gods in heaven and the rain that invigorates the earth. Verse 50, which is quoted from X.90.16, refers to the cycle of the sacrifice, which like the water cycle oper ates between heaven and earth. The sacrifice has its origins in heaven, but it is now performed on earth and directed back toward heaven. Such formal devices help maintain a sense of coherence in a hymn that covers substantial ritual and thematic territory.
We do not propose to discuss the verses of the hymn in detail, but we do want to provide some additional information and to illustrate especially the movement in this hymn between different levels of meaning. Verse 8 refers to the story of DawnтАЩs incest with her father, who is sometimes the Sun and sometimes Heaven. Depending on which of the two is her fatherтАФand either is possible in this verseтАФDawnтАЩs child might be the Sun or Agni, the ritual fire. Verse 14 describes the movement of the Sun, but here it is its movement at night, when its bright side is turned away from earth and it moves from the west to the east. Verse 15 continues the description of the night (cf. Thieme 1987). The seven who are born at the same time might be the seven stars of the constellation of the Seven Seers. Of these stars six are paired (15b) and one is single (╬╖ Ursae Majoris).
In verses 20тАУ22 is the famous riddle of the tree that has continued to remain a puzzle. The two birds have been interpreted as the waxing and waning moon (Thieme 1949: 55тАУ73) the moon and the sun (Kuiper 1970: 127тАУ28), the sun and the gharma pot (Houben 2000: 520тАУ22), and two seekers of knowledge (Geldner). Whatever the birds may be, the verse ultimately concerns the acquisition of knowl
edge or inspiration, the тАЬsweet figтАЭ (vs. 22) at the top of the tree. Given the enig matic character of this hymn, it is not surprising that this knowledge remains out of reach. Following the riddle of the two birds are three verses (23тАУ25) that present the development of ritual speech that perhaps embodies the knowledge represented in the тАЬsweet fig.тАЭ According to verse 23 g─Бyatr─л, triс╣гс╣нubh, and jagat─л lines are extracted from hymns composed in the g─Бyatr─л, triс╣гс╣нubh, and jagat─л meters. That is to say, the shorter constituent, the poetic line, is drawn from the larger, the whole poem. But then verse 24 begins with the g─Бyatr─л line, which is the basis for the тАЬchantтАЭ (arka╠Б), the hymn that is sung, and the chant is the basis of the тАЬmelodyтАЭ (s─Б╠Бman) on which many verses may be sung. If so, then this verse begins with the shortest constituent, the line, from which develop the longer songs and chants. Similarly, the triс╣гс╣нubh line is the basis for longer recitations, ┼Ыastras in the later tradition. The reason that the verse divides the chant and the recitation between the g─Бyatr─л and triс╣гс╣нubh lines is that the eight-syllable g─Бyatr─л line could be used as the basis for chants in the R╠еgvedic tradition, while the eleven-syllable triс╣гс╣нubh line was used in recitations. Thus in lines ab, reversing verse 23, the shorter (the chanted or recited line) is the basis for the longer (the chant or recitation). This order is continued in c, which moves from individual lines to the complete recitation. In d the shortest con stituent of all, the syllable, is the basis for the largest constituent, everything that is chanted or recited by the seven priests. This movement from long (the composed hymn) to short (the poetic line) to long (chants and recitations), and finally from shortest (the syllable) to longest (everything chanted or recited) knits together the entirety of ritual speech and ultimately concentrates it in the syllable. As such, these two verses anticipate verse 46, in which the тАЬOneтАЭ is the basis for many names. Verse 25 also presents the smallest constituent as the basis for the larger. According to it the g─Бyatr─л stanza is the foundation for the longer jagat─л stanza and the rathantara chant. The g─Бyatr─л verse is the basis of the jagat─л, because the jagat─л verse has twice the number of syllables as a g─Бyatr─л (48 and 24 respectively). It is the basis of the rathantara chant because the rathantara melody is set to VII.32.22тАУ23, verses in br╠еhat─л and satobr╠еhat─л meters. Verses in these two meters are combinations of jagat─л
and g─Бyatr─л lines. The g─Бyatr─л is thus the foundation of both the jagat─л and rathan tara and as such surpasses both of them.
The theme of inspired Speech (V─Бc) is taken up again in verses 36тАУ42. It is intro duced in verses 36 and 37, in which the poet shifts attention to ancient ┼Х╠ес╣гis тАЬseers,тАЭ whose тАЬinsightsтАЭ and тАЬthoughtтАЭ are brought into the present by poet. However, the poet does not understand his own inspiration (vs. 37), which is finally a gift of the gods or, more specifically, a gift of Agni. According to verses 39тАУ42, this inspired Speech descends to the human realm like water in order to sustain life on earth. While the emphasis in these verses is on Speech as a cosmic principle and human possession, a specific ritual reference is also not far away. As Geldner observes, verse 40 accompanies I.164.26тАУ27 in Atharvaveda ┼Ъaunaka 7.73, a hymn to the gharma drink of the Pravargya rite.
In verses 26тАУ29 the hymn focuses on the Pravargya rite. Verse 26 begins with the cow, whose milk will be the offering, and then describes the heating of the gharma pot, into which milk will be poured. In 27a the gharma pot makes a sound hiс╣Е as it is heated, and because it contains milk, the pot now becomes the cow. Her calf is probably Agni, an identification supported by 28ab, which can describe a pot placed on the fire. In verse 29 the meaning of the cow has shifted again, and she is now the milk тАЬenclosedтАЭ within the gharma pot. When milk is poured into the heated pot, a pillar of flame erupts in what is the most dramatic visual moment in the entire soma rite as now performed. In 29cd the milk or the cow thus becomes lightning, exploding upward from the pot. Although the reference to the Pravargya rite is less obvious in verse 30, the verse may refer to the boiling ghee in the gharma pot to which the milk is added (Houben 2000: 510) and therefore to an earlier stage of the ritual than does verse 29. HoubenтАЩs interpretation of verse 30 is partly based on the observation that verse 31 is the mantra prescribed by the ┼Ыrautas┼лtras for the rite of heating and gazing at the gharma pot, which also belongs to an earlier stage of the ritual. Houben may be correct in seeing a reference to the Pravargya rite, but both verses 30 and 31 are also open to additional interpretations. For example, the тАЬherdsmanтАЭ in 31a could be the breath (cf. Geldner; also Houben 2000: 508тАУ9) or the Sun (S─Бyaс╣Зa) or both.
Similarly, Houben (2000: 523) also explains verse 43 as reflecting the Pravargya rite. He understands the тАЬdung-smokeтАЭ to be smoke from the fire fueled by horse354 I.164
dung that is used to fumigate the gharma pot. The тАЬdappled bullockтАЭ could then be the mixture of milk and ghee that is heated in the gharma pot. But again, this verse can be more than a description of the Pravargya. The тАЬfirst foundationsтАЭ (p─Бda d) should refer not just to the beginning of a particular ritual performance, but to the institution of the sacrifice (cf. X.90), and therefore point to an addi
tional interpretation that locates the form and origin of the sacrifice in the cosmos. The тАЬmidpointтАЭ (viс╣г┼лva╠Бnt) can refer to the Viс╣г┼лvant day (as in I.84.10), the sum mer solstice, which is the ritual midpoint of a year-long sattra ceremony. This sug gests that the fire beyond the earthly fire is the sun, perhaps wrapped in cloud, the тАЬdung-smoke,тАЭ since the solstice should occur around the beginning of the rainy season. The sun can also be the тАЬbullock,тАЭ which is тАЬdappledтАЭ because of clouds or sunspots. The тАЬheroesтАЭ can be priests, but they may also be gods, who are gathered around the sun. All these ritual and macrocosmic interpretations are not exclusive since, according to the ─Аraс╣Зyakas and Br─Бhmaс╣Зas, the heated gharma pot can rep resent the sun (e.g., KauB VIII.3, T─А V.8тАУ9).
In verse 33 the Sun is the likely speaker, although GeldnerтАЩs idea that the speaker is the Wind and Breath would maintain the dual reference to cosmos and person. The imagery of these verses appears again in verse 38, in which the subject of lines ab may be the breath (Geldner) or the Sun. The image of the birth of an embryo in verse 33 leads to verses 34тАУ35, which speak of тАЬthe navel of the living worldтАЭ and the тАЬseedтАЭ or semen of the horse. These two verses form a brahmodya, a ritual exchange of question and answer, in the Horse Sacrifice (─А┼Ыv┼ЪS X.1тАУ3, ┼Ъ─Бс╣Еkh┼ЪS XVI.6.5тАУ6). The verses are appropriate to the Horse Sacrifice and may have been adopted into this hymn from that sacrifice. Here the verses continue the reference to heaven and earth and to the sacrifice, which becomes the image of the world.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI have beheld the Lord of men with seven sons; of which delightful and benevolent (deity), who is the object of our invocation, there is an all-pervading middle brother, and a third brother, well fed with (oblations of) ghee.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Seven sons: seven solar rays; ─Аditya, the seventh son of Aditi; a third brother: V_yu and Agni, the younger brothers of ─Аditya: Parame┼Ыvara = ─Аditya, the three sons refer to the attributes of Parame┼Ыvara of creating, preserving and destroying; The s┼лkta enunciates the doctrines of ved─Бnta, the spiritual unity of Brahm─Б and the universe; ─Аditya or the sun, is glorified aqnd identified with all creation. ┼Ъaunaka explains the s┼лkta at the level of repentance for a crime: if a br─Бhmaс╣Зa has committed theft, he may expiate the offence by fasting three nights and repeating the s┼лkta silently

This treasured one, the gray HotarтАФhis middle brother is the
ravenous one;
his third brother is the one with ghee-smeared back. In him I saw the clanlord with his seven sons.

OF this benignant Priest, with eld grey-coloured, the brother midmost of the three is lightning.
The third is he whose back with oil is sprinkled. Here I behold the Chief with seven male children.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey yoke the seven (horses) to the one-wheeled car; one horse, named seven, bears it along; the three-axled wheel is undecaying, never loosened, and in it all these regions of the universe abide.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

One-wheeled car: either the orb of the sun, or time, or a year; the seven horses may be the seven solar rays,or the six seasons, with their aggregation and year; or the six doublemonths, and the intercalary month; or the seven days of the week; the wheels of the car, as typical and identical are said to be one; one horse; eko a┼Ыvo saptan─Бma = the Sun or ─Аditya, either as the absorber of the seven flavours, or as praised by the seven с╣Ыс╣гi; it may be a pun, since sapta = a horse, seven; three-axled wheel: the day with its three sandhy─Бs; or time, past, present and fugure; all these regions: all things are dependent upon time, which of itself is imperishable: an─Бdinidhanaс╕е k─Бlaс╕е, time is without beginning or end

+Jamison Brereton

The seven harness the chariot with a single wheel [=the Sun]. A single horse with seven names draws it.
Triple-naved [=with three seasons?] is the unaging, unassailable wheel, on which all these living beings rest.

+Griffith

Seven to the one-wheeled chariot yoke the Courser; bearing seven names the single Courser draws it.
Three-naved the wheel is, sound and undecaying, whereon are resting all these worlds of being.

+Geldner

Sieben schirren den einr├дdrigen Wagen an; ein Pferd zieht ihn, das sieben Namen hat. Dreinabig, niemals altersschwach, un├╝bertroffen ist das Rad, auf dem alle diese Wesen stehen.

+Grassmann

Sieben [Priester] schirren den einr├дdrigen Wagen [die Sonne]; ein Ross, das sieben Namen f├╝hrt, zieht ihn; drei Naben [die drei Tageszeiten] hat das Rad, das nicht alternde, unaufhaltsame, auf welches alle diese Wesen steigen.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe seven who preside over this sevenpwheeled chariot (are) the seven horses who draw it; seven sisters ride in it together, and in are deposited the seven forms of utterance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The seven: either the solar rays or the seven portions of a year: ayana (solstine season), month, fortnight, day, night, hour; seven horses: seven wheels and seven horses are the seven solar rays; seven sisters: either the rays of the run, or the six seasons and the aggregate year of the six double and one intercalary month; seven forms of utterance: seven notes of music as employed in chanting the praises of the Sun; or, if gav─Бm is used in the sense of water, the seven forms may be the seven divine rivers

+Jamison Brereton

As its seven horses, the seven [=the priests] who stand upon this chariot [=the sacrifice] draw the seven-wheeled (chariot).
Seven sisters [=voices of the priests] together cry out (the words) in
which the seven names of the cows [=poetic speech] are imprinted.

+Griffith

The seven who on the seven-wheeled car are mounted have horses, seven in tale, who draw them onward.
Seven Sisters utter songs of praise together, in whom the names of the seven Cows are treasured.

+Geldner

W├дhrend sieben diesen Wagen bestiegen haben, ziehen sieben Rosse den siebenr├дdrigen Wagen. Sieben Schwestern schreien ihm zu, in dem die sieben Namen der K├╝he niedergelegt sind.

+Grassmann

Diesen Wagen [wol wieder die Sonne, aber in ihrem Jahreslauf betrachtet?], welchen [j├бm statt j├й?] die sieben bestiegen haben, den siebenr├дdrigen, ziehen sieben Rosse; sieben Schwestern [wol die in der Luft gedachten Str├╢me] rauschen ihm entgegen, dort wo die sieben Namen der K├╝he eingesetzt sind.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWho has seen the primeval (being) at the time of his being born; what is that endowed with substance which the unsubstantial sustains; from earth are the breath and blood; but where is the soul; who may repair to the sage to ask this?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Tha endowed with subtance: asthanvantam yad anasth─Б bibharti = liс╣н, that which having bone the boneless sustains; the boneless is the prakс╣Ыti of the s─Бс╣Еkhya, or the m─Бy─Б of the ved─Бntins, which is formless matter, or spiritual illusion, from which the material and visible world proceeds; where is the soul: bh┼лmy─Б asur-asс╣Ыg-─Бtm─Б kva svit: bh┼лmi = sth┼лla ┼Ыar─лra, gross body;

Asuс╕е = breath, the s┼лkс╣гma ┼Ыar─лra, or suble body;

Asс╣Ыj = blood, the aggregate elements of which the body is formed; ─Бtm─Б or cetan─Б, the thinking principle, although connected with gross and subtle form, is nowhere perceptible as a separate object, and not to be apprehended, either by pupil or teacher

+Jamison Brereton

Who has seen the first one [=the Sun/Agni] as he is being born, when his boneless (mother) [=the Waters?] carries the one having bones [=the one who is a living being]?
Where is the life, blood, and breath of the earth? Who will approach the knowing one to ask this?

+Griffith

Who hath beheld him as he sprang to being, seen how the boneless One supports the bony?
Where is the blood of earth, the life, the spirit? Who may approach the man who knows, to ask it?

+Geldner

Wer hat den zuerst Geborenen gesehen, da die Knochenlose den Knochigen tr├дgt? Wo ist denn der Erde Lebensgeist, Blut und Seele? Wer trifft einen Wissenden um danach zu fragen?

+Grassmann

Wer hat den zuerst geborenen Knochenbegabten [das Urwesen] gesehen, wenn ihn der knochenlose [Himmel oder Erdboden oder beides vereint im Chaos] tr├дgt? Wo ist doch der Erde Athem, Blut, Seele? Wer mag zu dem wissenden gehen, dies zu erfragen?

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬImmature (in understanding) undiscerning in mind, I inquire of those things which are hidden (even) from the gods; (what are) the seven threads which the sages have spread to envelop the sun, in whom all abide?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Immature: p─Бkaс╕е = lit. ripening, being or making mature; here, it is equated with paktavyaс╕е, what is to be matured; apakvamatiraham, I of immature mind; seven threads: sapta tant┼лn = seven forms of the soma sacrifice, or the seven metres of the vedas; the seen: vatse baс╣гkaye adhi: vatse = sarvasya niv─Бsa bh┼лte;

Baс╣гkaye = ─Бditye; the lit. meaning is, a yearling calf, just as vatsa also means a calf; the term vatse is already used, hence, baс╣гkaya = time or the sun

+Jamison Brereton

Nai╠Иve, not understanding, in my mind I ask about these imprinted tracks of the gods.
Upon the full-grown calf [=the fire] the poets have stretched the seven warp-threads (of the sacrifice) in order to weave.

+Griffith

Unripe in mind, in spirit undiscerning, I ask of these the Gods’ established places;
For up above the yearling Calf the sages, to form a web, their own seven threads have woven.

+Geldner

Als Tor, der in seinem Verstand sich nicht auskennt, frage ich nach den darin hinterlassenen Spuren der G├╢tter. An dem ausgewachsenen Kalbe zogen die sieben Seher sieben F├дden auf, um daran zu weben.

+Grassmann

Ich unkundiger frage, mit meinem Geiste es nicht erkennend, nach diesen eingesetzten St├дtten der G├╢tter; ├╝ber dem einj├дhrigen Kalbe [der Sonne in ihrem Jahreslauf] spannten die weisen [G├╢tter] sieben F├дden aus zum Weben [wol die sieben Jahresopfer eines Opfercyklus].

+Elizarenkova

рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реНрд░реБрддреЗрдГ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIgnorant, I inquire of the sages who know (the truth); not as one knowing (do I inquire), for the sake of (gaining) knowledge; what is that one alone, who has upheld these six spheres in the form of the unborn?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

What is that one alone: yas tastambha ┼Ыad im─Б raj─Бс╣Гsi ajasya r┼лpe kim apisvidekam: the ‘one’ is: 1) the orb of the ungenerated sun on which the six seasons depend; 2) satyaloka, whence there is no return, the stay of the other six worlds or regions; 3) the sole form of the unborn creator

+Jamison Brereton

Unperceptive, I ask also the perceptive poets about this in order to know, since I am unknowing:
What also is the One in the form of the Unborn [=the Sun] that has propped apart these six realms (of heaven and earth)?

+Griffith

I ask, unknowing, those who know, the sages, as one all ignorant for sake of knowledge,
What was that ONE who in the Unborn’s image hath stablished and fixed firm these worlds’ six regions.

+Geldner

Als Unkundiger befrage ich dar├╝ber die kundigen Seher um es zu wissen, selbst nicht wissend. Was ist denn ferner das Eine in Gestalt des Ungeborenen, der diese sechs Weltr├дume auseinander gestemmt hat?

+Grassmann

Es nicht erkennend frage ich hier die erkennenden weisen aus, um es zu wissen, da ich es nicht weiss. Welcher diese sechs R├дume [nach den sechs Weltrichtungen] ausspannte in der Gestalt des ungeborenen, was ist doch recht dies eine?

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLet him who knows this (truth) quickly declare it; the mysterious condition of the beautiful ever-moving (sun); the rays shed (their) milk from his (exalted) head investing his form with radiance; they have drunk up the water by the paths (by which they were poured forth).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By the paths: the solar rays, which sedn down rain and also reabsorb water

+Jamison Brereton

Let him speak here, who knows the imprinted track of this treasured bird [=the Sun].
The cows [=rain clouds] yield milk [=rain] from his head [=the Sun]. Clothing themselves in a cloak, they have drunk water with the foot [=the SunтАЩs rays].

+Griffith

Let him who knoweth presently declare it, this lovely Bird’s securely founded station.
Forth from his head the Cows draw milk, and, wearing his vesture, with their foot have drunk the water.

+Geldner

Hier soll sie sagen, wer sie gewi├Я kennt, die hinterlassene Spur dieses liebwerten Vogels. Aus seinem Haupte geben die K├╝he Milch. K├╢rperform annehmend haben sie das Wasser mit dem Fu├Я getrunken.

+Grassmann

Hier m├╢ge der, welcher es recht weiss, dieses sch├╢nen Vogels [der Sonne] niedergesetzten Fuss nennen; aus seinem Haupte melken sich Milch die K├╝he [die Wolken], in ihr Gewand, das Wasser, gekleidet, erreichten (─Бpus, Padap. apus) sie seine St├дtten.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe mother, (earth), worships the father, (sun), with holy rites, for the sake of water; but he has anticipated (her wants) in his mind; whereupon desirous of progeny, she is penetrated by the dews of impregnation, and, (all) expectant of abundance, exchange words (of congratulation).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Exchange words: metaphocial account of the agency of the sun sending rain upon the earth and its consequent fertility

+Jamison Brereton

The mother [=Dawn] gave her father [=the Sun/Heaven] a share in the truth, for in the beginning, through her insight, she united (with him) by her mind.
Recoiling, she whose essence was her child [=Agni/the Sun] was pierced (by her father). Just those offering their reverence went to the
(morning) invocation.

+Griffith

The Mother gave the Sire his share of Order: with thought, at first, she wedded him in spirit.
She, the coy Dame, was filled with dew prolific: with adoration men approached to praise her.

+Geldner

Die Mutter macht den Vater seines Rechtes teilhaft, denn sie hatte sich zuvor in ihrem Sinnen und Denken mit ihm geeinigt. Die Spr├╢de ward durchbohrt, von Feuchtigkeit befruchtet. Ehrfurchtsvoll kamen sie ihn zu ermuntern.

+Grassmann

Die Mutter [das Urbild der Erde] machte den Vater [den Himmel als Geist gedacht] theilhaft des geb├╝hrenden Werkes; denn durch Denken verm├дhlte sie sich zuerst mit dem Geiste; sie, die spr├╢de, als sie durchbohrt war [vermittels des Zeugungsactes], war angef├╝llt mit schw├дngernder Feuchtigkeit; da begannen die Andachtsvollen zu preisen.

+Elizarenkova

рдорд╛рддрд╛ ред рдирд┐рд░реНрдореАрдпрдиреНрддреЗ рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рднреВрддрд╛рдиреАрддрд┐ рдорд╛рддрд╛ рджреНрдпреМрдГ ред рджрдХреНрд╖рд┐рдгрд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдЕрднрд┐рдорддрдкреВрд░рдгрд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рдпрд╛рдГ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рдГ рдзреБрд░рд┐ рдирд┐рд░реНрд╡рд╣рдгреЗ рдпреБрдХреНрддрд╛ рдЖрд╕реАрддреН рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рд╕рдорд░реНрдерд╛рднреВрджрд┐рддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдХрдердорд┐рддрд┐ рддрджреБрдЪреНрдпрддреЗ ред рдЧрд░реНрднрдГ рдЧрд░реНрднрд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╕рдВрдШрдГ рд╡реГрдЬрдиреАрд╖реБ рдЙрджрдХрд╡рддреНрд╕реБ рдореЗрдШрдкрдЩреНрдХреНрддрд┐рд╖реБ рдЕрдиреНрддрдГ рдордзреНрдпреЗ рдЕрддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддреН рддрд┐рд╖реНрдарддрд┐ ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╡рддреНрд╕рдГ рдкреБрддреНрд░рд╕реНрдерд╛рдиреАрдпрдГ рдЙрджрдХрд╕рдВрдШрдГ рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдпреЛрдЬрдиреЗрд╖реБ рдореЗрдШрд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╖реБ рд╕рдВрдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рддреНрд╕реБ рдЕрдореАрдореЗрддреН рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрд╕рдордпреЗ рд╢рдмреНрджрдпрддрд┐ ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреНрдпрдВ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкрд╡рддреАрдВ рдЧрд╛рдореН рдЕрдиреБ рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрддреН рдЕрдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рдкрд╢реНрдпрддрд┐ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рддреАрддреНрдпрд░реНрдердГ ред рдпрджреНрд╡рд╛ ред рддреНрд░рд┐рд╖реБ рдпреЛрдЬрдиреЗрд╖реБ рд╕рддреНрд╕реБ рд╡рддреНрд╕реЛ рдореЗрдШреЛ рд╡рд░реНрд╖рдгрд╛рдп рдЧрд╛рдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐ рдЕрдореАрдореЗрддреН ред рдЕрдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЛ рдЬрдиреЛрд╜рдиреБрдХреНрд░рдореЗрдг рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд░реВрдкреНрдпрдВ рд╕рд╕реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рднрд┐рд░реНрдирд╛рдирд╛рд░реВрдкрд╡рддреАрдВ рднреВрдорд┐рдореН рдЕрдкрд╢реНрдпрддреН рдкрд╢реНрдпрддрд┐ рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe mother, (sky), was associated in (sustaining) the burden of the fulfiller of desires, (the earth); the embryo (water) rested within the (womb of the) clouds; thereupon the calf bellowed, and beheld the omniform cow in the three combinations.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The calf bellowed: the cloud thundered; the omniform cow: vi┼Ыvar┼лpyam g─Бm triс╣гu yojaneс╣гu = the earth diversified by various crops in consequence of the co-operation of the cloud, the wind, and the rays of the sun

+Jamison Brereton

The mother was harnessed to the yoke-pole of the sacrificial reward; her child stood up amid the penned cows.
The calf [=Agni] bellowed and looked toward the cow of every color [=Dawn], three wagon-treks (in the distance).

+Griffith

Yoked was the Mother to the boon Cow’s car-pole: in the dank rows of cloud the Infant rested.
Then the Calf lowed, and looked upon the Mother, the Cow who wears all shapes in three directions.

+Geldner

Die Mutter war ins Joch der Daksina eingespannt, das Kind stand unter den …….. Das Kalb br├╝llte, es sah sich nach der Kuh um, nach der allfarbigen drei Wegstrecken weit.

+Grassmann

Die Mutter war geschirrt an die Deichsel der reichlich milchenden Kuh [etwa des Opfers?], der neugeborene [wol Feuer und Sonne als eins gedacht] stand da mitten unter den Wolkenk├╝hen; es br├╝llte das Kalb, es blickte hin zu der vielgestaltigen Mutterkuh drei Strecken weit [Morgen, Mittag, Abend].

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe one sole (sun), having three mothers and three fathers, stood on high; none ever over-weary him; the (gods) on the summit of the sky take counsel respecting him in language all-comprehending (but) not extending to all.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Three mothers and three fathers: the three worlds, earth, sky, heaven; and the three deities presiding over them: agni, v─Бyu, s┼лrya; in language: vi┼Ыvavidam v─Бcam avi┼Ыvaminv─Бm = speech or discourse, knowing all, or which may be known by all; or, that which does not extend to all, a-sarvavy─Бpin─лm;

Speech = thunder: v─Бcam garjitalakс╣гaс╣Зam

+Jamison Brereton

Carrying three mothers [=earths] and three fathers [=heavens] alone, he [=the Sun] stands upright: they do not cause him to weary.
On the back of yonder heaven they [=the gods] recite the speech that knows everything but does not inspire everyone.

+Griffith

Bearing three Mothers and three Fathers, single he stood erect: they never make him weary.
There on the pitch of heaven they speak together in speech all-knowing but not all-impelling.

+Geldner

Drei M├╝tter, drei V├дter tr├дgt der Eine und steht doch aufrecht da; nicht ermatten sie ihn. Auf dem R├╝cken jenes Himmels ersinnen sie die allwissende Rede, die nicht einen jeden bewegt.

+Grassmann

Er stand allein aufrecht tragend die drei M├╝tter und die drei V├дter [die drei Erden und die drei Himmel], nicht erm├╝den sie ihn; auf dem R├╝cken jenes Himmels sprechen sie den alles Wissen enthaltenden, nicht ├╝berall hindringenden Spruch.

+Elizarenkova

рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рд░рдгреНрдпрдХрдореН рее

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe twelve-spoked wheel, of the true (sun) revolves round the heavens, and never (tends) to decay; seven hundred and twenty children in pais, Agni, abide in it.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Twelve-spoked wheel: the twelve signs of the zodiac: dv─Бda┼Ы─Бram dv─Бda┼Ыa saс╣Еkhy─Бkameс╣г─Бdir─Б┼Ыy─Бtmakaiс╕е m─Бs─Бtmakairv─Б araiс╕е rath─Бс╣Еg─Бvayavayairyuktam; the term may also mean twelve months; seven hundred and twenty children: nights and days; three hundred and sixty of each: sapta ca vai ┼Ыat─Бni viс╣Г┼Ыati┼Ыca saс╣Гvatsarasy─Бhor─Бtr─Бс╕е sa eс╣гohaс╕е smm─Бnaс╕е (Aitareya ─Аraс╣Зyaka 3.2.1)

+Jamison Brereton

Twelve-spoked, the wheel of truth [=the Sun] ever rolls around
heavenтАФyet not to old age.
Upon it, o Agni, stand seven hundred twenty sons in pairs [=the nights and days of the year].

+Griffith

Formed with twelve spokes, by length of time, unweakened, rolls round the heaven this wheel of during Order.
Herein established, joined in pairs together, seven hundred Sons and twenty stand, O Agni.

+Geldner

Dies zw├╢lfspeichige Rad der Zeitordnung dreht sich immer wieder um den Himmel, denn nicht kann es sich abnutzen. Darauf stehen, o Agni, die S├╢hne paarweise, siebenhundert und zwanzig.

+Grassmann

Denn ohne sich je abzunutzen rollt das zw├╢lfspeichige Rad der ewigen Ordnung [das Jahr] um den Himmel, siebenhundertundzwanzig verzwillingte S├╢hne [360 Tage und N├дchte], o Agni, sind auf das selbe hinaufgestiegen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey have termed the five-footed, twelve-formed parent, Puriс╣гin, when in the further hemisphere of the sky; and others have termed in Arpita, when in the hither (portion of the sky); shining in his seven-wheeled car), each (wheel) having six spokes.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Puriс╣гin: from puriс╣гa, water;

Puriс╣гin = the sun, as the source of rain; the first five feet are the five seasons, the dewy and cold seasons forming one; the twelve forms are the twelve months, or twelve ─Бdityas;

Arpita = adh─лnam or par─Бyattam, dependent upon, and applicable to the sun, as dependent upon, or influenced by, the course of the year, or recurrence of the solstices; moving quick or slow according to his southern or northern declination; in the hither portion of the sky: upare = where living creatures are delighted–uparamanta asmin pr─Бс╣Зinaс╕е; or, it may mean a year, v─Б saс╣Гvatsaraс╕е; it may be related to the first line of the hymn: divaс╕е pare ardhe, in the further part of the sky; upara may imply the nearer or hither part, referring to the two ayanas, or solstices; the seven wheels are the seven rays, or the seven days of the week, the six spokes are the six seasona

+Jamison Brereton

They speak of the father [=the Moon] with five feet [=the seasons] and twelve forms [=the months], the overflowing one in the upper half of heaven.
But these others speak of the far-gazing one [=the Sun] in the nearer (half) fixed on (the chariot) with seven wheels [=the Sun, Moon,
and visible planets] and six spokes [=the seasons, in a different
reckoning].

+Griffith

They call him in the farther half of heaven the Sire five-footed, of twelve forms, wealthy in watery store.
These others say that he, God with far-seeing eyes, is mounted on the lower seven-wheeled, six-spoked car.

+Geldner

Sie bezeichnen als Vater den f├╝nff├╝├Яigen, zw├╢lfteiligen, der auf der entfernten Seite des Himmels im Vollen sitzt. Aber diese anderen sagen, da├Я es der Hellsichtige auf der unteren Seite sei, der auf den siebenr├дdrigen sechsspeichigen Wagen gesetzt ist.

+Grassmann

F├╝nff├╝ssig, sagen sie, sei der zw├╢lftheilige Vater, der an Feuchtigkeit reiche am entfernten R├дume des Himmels [wol sich auf die f├╝nf feuchten Monate beziehend?], und diese andern sagen, der weithinleuchtende sei an dem unteren siebenr├дdrigen, sechsspeichigen eingef├╝gt [auf die sieben trockenen Monate sich beziehend, die sechs Speichen etwa auf die sechs Jahreszeiten?].

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬAll beings abide in this five-spoked revolving wheel; the heavily-loaded axle is never heated; its eternal compact nave is never worn away.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Five-spoked wheel: the five seasons; or the cycle of five years

+Jamison Brereton

In the five-spoked wheel [=the year] that rolls roundтАФon that do all living beings take their stand.
Its axle does not become hot, though its load is heavy. From of old it, along with its nave, does not break apart.

+Griffith

Upon this five-spoked wheel revolving ever all living creatures rest and are dependent.
Its axle, heavy-laden, is not heated: the nave from ancient time remains unbroken.

+Geldner

Auf dem f├╝nfspeichigen Rade, das sich im Kreis dreht, auf dem stehen alle Wesen. Seine Achse wird nicht hei├Я, obwohl sie viele Lasten tr├дgt. Seit alters bricht sie nicht mitsamt der Nabe.

+Grassmann

Auf diesem f├╝nfspeichigen, sich drehenden Rade stehen alle Wesen; seine vieltragende Achse erhitzt sich nicht; von Alters her wird sie nicht abgenutzt durch den Lauf der Zeiten.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe even-fellied, undecaying wheel, repeatedly revolves; ten, united on the upper surface, bear (the world); the orb of the sun proceeds, invested with water, and in it are all beings deposited.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ten: the ten organs of sense, or he five lokap─Бlas, guardians of the world, and five classes of human beings; upper surface: utt─Бn─Бy─Бm, or the upper part; ┼лrdhvatan─Бy─Бm, or the pole, ─лс╣г─Бy─Бm; or the earth spread above, upar─л vistс╣Ыta bh_my─Бm; the orb of the sun: s┼лryasya cakс╣гus. = liс╣н, the eye of the sun, either the display of the nature or radiance of the sun, or his orb, being, as it were, the eye of all; sarvasya cakс╣гuс╕е sth─Бn─лyam v─Б maс╣Зс╕Нalam

+Jamison Brereton

Along with its felly, the unaging wheel [=the night Sun] has turned away. Harnessed to the outstretched (yoke-pole) [=the airy realm?], ten (horses) draw it.
Covered over, the eye of the Sun moves through the airy realm. All living beings are fixed upon it.

+Griffith

The wheel revolves, unwasting, with its felly: ten draw it, yoked to the far-stretching car-pole.
The Sun’s eye moves encompassed by the region: on him dependent rest all living creatures.

+Geldner

Das Rad dreht sich ohne abzunutzen mitsamt der Felge; zehn ziehen an die waagerechte Deichsel angespannt. Das Auge der Sonne geht, auch wenn es in Dunst geh├╝llt ist. Darauf sind alle Wesen gesetzt.

+Grassmann

Das mit Radkranz versehene, nicht morsch werdende Rad dreht sich herum, an der ausgestreckten Deichsel ziehen zehn angeschirrte Rosse; das Auge der Sonne geht von dem dunklen Luftraume umgeben; in ihm sind alle Wesen eingef├╝gt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬOf those that are born together, sages have called the seventh single-born; for six are twins, and are moveable, and born of the gods; their desirable (properties), plural ced severally in their proper abode, are various (also) in form, and revolve for (the benefit of) that which is stationary.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Six are twins: six seasons, made of two months each; the seventh is the intercalary month, which has no ─Бditya to preside over it; the six seasons are also с╣Ыsi, с╣Ыс╣гayaс╕е = gant─Бraс╕е, goers; a с╣Ыс╣гi is present in the sun’s car in each of the twelve months; revolve for the benefit: the seasons are diversified by classes of temperature, produce, for the benefit of the world

+Jamison Brereton

They speak of the seventh of those who are born at the same time as the one born alone, saying, тАЬthe twins, the Seers born of the gods, are only six.тАЭ
What (places) are desired by these [=the Seven Seers] are distributed according to their spheres. While (the one) [=the pole star] stands still, the ones varied in appearance [=the stars of the Seven Seers] quiver.

+Griffith

Of the co-born they call the seventh single-born; the six twin pairs are called Rsis, Children of Gods.
Their good gifts sought of men are ranged in order due, and various in their form move for the Lord who guides.

+Geldner

Sie sagen, da├Я der Siebente unter den Paarweise geborenen ein Einling ist. Sechs sind Zwillinge, gottgeborene Rishi┬┤s werden sie genannt. Deren liebe, nach der Ordnung festgestellte Tage bewegen sich zitternd wie die Speichen, w├дhrend er feststeht, indem sie sich der Form nach ver├дndern.

+Grassmann

Von den zugleich erzeugten [Jahreszeiten] nennen sie die siebente [den Schaltmonat] die einzeln geborene [sofern sie nur aus einem Monat besteht], die sechs gepaarten [sofern jede von ihnen aus zwei Monaten besteht] nennen die Weisen ┬╗die von den G├╢ttern erzeugten┬л, unter diesen sind die erw├╝nschten nach der Ordnung vertheilt, an ihrem Standorte regen sie sich verschiedengestaltet je nach ihrer Art.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey have called thes, my virtuous feminine les, males; he who has eyes beholds; the blind man sees not; he whois a sage son understands this, and he who discriminates is the father of the father.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Males: an instrumental nce of grammatical mysticism: ra┼Ыmi, a ray of the sun, is here person nified as a feminine le, is properly a noun masculine; the father of the father: the sun is to be considered as the father of the rays of light, which are the cause of rain, or the fosterers or parent of the earth; the sun is, therefore, the father of the father, and he who knows this is identical with the sun

+Jamison Brereton

Though they [=the Kr╠еttik─Бs, the Pleiades] are women, yet they speak of them as men to me. He who has eyes sees; the blind man does not differentiate.
One who is a poet, a (poetтАЩs) son, perceives them. One who recognizes these (women), he will be the father of his father.

+Griffith

They told me these were males, though truly females: he who hath eyes sees this, the blind discerns not.
The son who is a sage hath comprehended: who knows this rightly is his father’s father.

+Geldner

Die eigentlich Frau sind, bezeichnen sie mir als M├дnner. Wer Augen hat, sieht sie; nicht err├дt es der Blinde. Der Sohn, der ein Seher ist, der kennt sie. Wer diese err├дt, der soll der Vater des Vaters sein.

+Grassmann

Welche Weiber sind [N├дchte und Morgenr├╢then?], die nannten sie mir M├дnner [Tage?], sehen kann sie der mit Augen begabte, der Blinde kann sie nicht unterscheiden. Der Sohn, welcher weise ist, der hat es erwogen; wer dies ganz erkennt, der kann des Vaters Vater sein [soll wol heissen: von dem kann noch sein Vater lernen].

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe cow, holding her calf underneath with her fore-feet, and then above with her hind-feet, has risen up; whither is she gone; to whom has she turned back when half-way; where does she bear young; it is not amidst the herd.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cow is the burnt-offering and the calf is Agni and the positions of the two indicate the station of the offerer with respect to the sun; or, the cow may typify the solar rays collectively and the calf the worshipper

+Jamison Brereton

Below the upper (realm), above the lower here [=at the horizon], the cow [=Dawn] carrying her calf [=the Sun] has stood up by her foot. In which direction is she? Toward which side did she go away? Where does she give birth, for it is not within the fold?

+Griffith

Beneath the upper realm, above this lower, bearing her calf at foot the Cow hath risen.
Witherward, to what place hath she departed? Where calves she? Not amid this herd of cattle.

+Geldner

Unterhalb des jenseitigen Raumes, jenseits dieses unteren hat sich die Kuh erhoben, die mit ihrem Fu├Я ein Kalb tr├дgt. Wohin hat sie sich gewendet? Nach welcher Seite ist sie verzogen? Wo gebiert sie denn? Denn sie ist nicht in der Herde.

+Grassmann

Unter dem h├╢heren Raum [Himmel] ├╝ber diesem niederen [der Erde], am Fusse das Kalb [die Sonne] f├╝hrend, ist die Kuh [die Morgenr├╢the] emporgestiegen; wohin hat sie sich gewandt? nach welcher Gegend hin ist sie fortgegangen? wo gebiert sie? denn nicht geschieht es innerhalb der Heerde.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe who knows the protector of this (world) as the inferior associated with the superior, and the superior associated with the inferior, he is, as it were, a sage; but who in this world can expound (it); whence is the divine mind in its supremacy engendereс╕НтАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Below the upper (realm), above the lower here is he [=the Sun] who knows his father.
Showing himself to be a poet, who will proclaim this here: from whence has divine thought been born?

+Griffith

Who, that the father of this Calf discerneth beneath the upper realm, above the lower,
Showing himself a sage, may here declare it? Whence hath the Godlike spirit had its rising?

+Geldner

Wer, der den Vater dieses Kalbes unterhalb des jenseitigen Raumes, jenseits dieses unteren kennt, kann es hier verk├╝nden, als Seher sich erweisend, woher der g├╢ttliche Geist entsprungen ist?

+Grassmann

Wer dieses Kalbes Vater unter dem h├╢heren Raume ├╝ber diesem niederen recht erkennt, als weisester, wer mag es uns hier verk├╝nden? von wo ist der g├╢ttliche Urgeist entsprungen?

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThose which (the sages) have termed descending, they have also termed ascending; and those they have termed ascending, they have also called descending; and those (orbits) which your, Soma and Indra, have made, bear along the worlds like (oxen) yoked to a twain.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those which: the rays of light, or the plural nets changing their relative position as they revolve; Soma and Indra: the moon and the sun; Indra is one of the twelve ─Аdityas or identical here with the sun

+Jamison Brereton

What (chariots [=sacrifices?] come) this wayтАФthey say that those (will go) away; what (chariots go) awayтАФthey say that those (will come) this way.
O Soma and Indra, (the deeds) that you two have done, these draw (those chariots) like (horses) harnessed to the yoke-pole of the
airy realm.

+Griffith

Those that come hitherward they call departing, those that depart they call directed hither.
And what so ye have made, Indra and Soma, steeds bear as ’twere yoked to the region’s car-pole.

+Geldner

Die kommenden nennen sie die Gehenden, die Gehenden nennen sie die wieder Kommenden. Die ihr beide, Soma und du Indra, geschaffen habt, die ziehen am Joche der Welt wie angeschirrte Rosse.

+Grassmann

Welche [Tage] hinterw├дrst stehen, die nennen sie die fr├╝heren, und welche vor den andern stehen, die nennen sie die sp├дtern, und welche [Tageshellen] ihr, o Indra und Soma, geschaffen habt, die werden gefahren von den gleichsam an die Deichsel des Luftraums geschirrten.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬTwo birds associated together, and mutual friends, take refuge in the same tree; one of them eats the sweet fig; the other abstaining from food, merely looks on.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Two birds associated together: the vital and supreme spirit, jiv─Бtm─Б and param─Бtm─Б, are here alluded to using the metaphor of the two birds; eats the sweet fig: pippalam sv─Бdu atti: the vital spirit enjoys the rewards of acts. dvau dvau pratiс╣гс╣нhitau sukс╣Ыtau dharmakart─Бrau: two species of souls to be intended as abiding in one body (Nirukta 14.30)

+Jamison Brereton

Two well-feathered (birds), yokemates and companions, embrace the same tree.
Of those two the one eats the sweet fig; the other, not eating,
keeps watch.

+Griffith

Two Birds with fair wings, knit with bonds of friendship, in the same sheltering tree have found a refuge.
One of the twain eats the sweet Fig-tree’s fruitage; the other eating not regardeth only.

+Geldner

Zwei V├╢gel, eng verbundene Kameraden, umklammern den gleichen Baum. Der eine von ihnen i├Яt die s├╝├Яe Beere, der andere schaut ohne zu essen zu.

+Grassmann

Zwei sch├╢ngefl├╝gelte zusammengeschirrte Genossen [Tag und Nacht] umschlingen denselben Baum [die Welt], von diesen beiden geniesst der eine [der Tag] die s├╝sse Frucht, der andre beschaut sie, ohne zu geniessen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWhere the smooth-gliding (rays), cognizant (of their duty), distil the perpetual portion of ambrosia (water); there has the lord and steadfast protector all beings consigned me, (though) immature (in wisdom).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Smooth-gliding: supraс╣Зa = supatanaс╕е ┼Ыobhana gamana ra┼Ыmayaс╕е, the goers easily or beautifully, the rays of the sun; consigned me: ─Аditya has admitted, or admits me, the reciter of the hymn, to the sphere of the sun

+Jamison Brereton

Where the well-feathered (birds), never blinking, cry out for a share of immortality and for the ritual distributions,
here the forceful herdsman of the whole living world, the insightful one, has entered me, the nai╠Иve one.

+Griffith

Where those fine Birds hymn ceaselessly their portion of life eternal, and the sacred synods,
There is the Universe’s mighty Keeper, who, wise, hath entered into me the simple.

+Geldner

Dort, wo die V├╢gel, ohne zu ruhen, nach einem Anteil an der Unsterblichkeit, nach Weisheit schreien, da ist der m├дchtige H├╝ter der ganzen Welt, der Weise in mich Toren eingegangen.

+Grassmann

Wo die beiden sch├╢ngefl├╝gelten dem Antheil an dem Unsterblichkeitstranke und den versammelten Scharen [der Opferer?] schlummerlos entgegenrauschen, da ist der m├дchtige H├╝ter der ganzen Welt, er, der weise, zu mir, dem th├╢richten, eingegangen.

+Elizarenkova

рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдХрд╛ рддреБ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рдирд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрддрд┐рдорд╛рд╣ ред рддрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдИрджреГрд╢рдВ рдкрд░рдореЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдВ рд╡рд┐рджрд┐рддреНрд╡рд╛ +Wilson
English translation:

тАЬIn the tree into which the smooth-gliding (rays) feeders on the sweet (produce), enter, and again bring forth (light) over all, they have called the fruit sweet, but he partakes not of it who knows not the protector (of the universe).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The tree: the orb or region of the sun; he partakes not of it, who: tan na unna ┼Ыad yaс╕е pitaram na veda: pitaram = p─Бlaka, cherisher, protector; the sun, the supreme spirit

+Jamison Brereton

Just that tree on which all the honey-eating, well-feathered ones settle and give birth,
they say, has the sweet fig at its top. He who does not know the father will not reach up to that.

+Griffith

The, tree whereon the fine Birds eat the sweetness, where they all rest and procreate their offspring,–
Upon its top they say the fig is luscious none gaineth it who knoweth not the Father.

+Geldner

Wo die s├╝├Яe Frucht essenden V├╢gel alle nisten und ausbr├╝ten, im Wipfel dieses Baumes ist, wie sie sagen, die s├╝├Яe Beere. Zu der langt nicht hinan, wer nicht den Vater kennt.

+Grassmann

Auf welchem Baume die sch├╢ngefl├╝gelten, welche die s├╝sse Frucht geniessen, alle sich niederlassen und nisten, an dessen Gipfel, sagt man, sei die s├╝sse Feige; diese kann niemand erreichen, der den Vater nicht kennt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThey who know the station of Agni upon the earth; the station of V─Бyu that was fabricated from the firmament; and that station of the Sun which is plural ced in heaven, obtain immortality.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Yadg─Бyatre adhi g─Бyatram traс╣гс╣нubh─Бd v─Б traiс╣гс╣нubham: perhaps, a mystical reference to the text of the Veda, a knowledge of which is essential to final felicity; g─Бyatra is derived from g─Бyatr─л the earth; it is the pada, or station of Agni; traiс╣гс╣нubha is identified with the firmament, and the plural ce of V─Бyu; j─Бgat is identified with the sun: j─Бgat, the solar region (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 2.2.9.5-6)

+Jamison Brereton

How the g─Бyatr─л (track) [=g─Бyatr─л line] is based upon a g─Бyatr─л (hymn) or how a triс╣гс╣нubh (track) [=triс╣гс╣нubh line] was fashioned out of a triс╣гс╣нubh (hymn),
or how the jagat track [=jagat─л line] is based on the jagat [=jagat─л]
(hymn)тАФonly those who know this have reached immortality.

+Griffith

How on the Gayatri the Gayatri was based, how from the Tristup they fashioned the Tristup forth,
How on the Jagati was based the Jagati,–they who know this have won themselves immortal life.

+Geldner

Nur die haben die Unsterblichkeit erlangt, die wissen, da├Я der Gayatrifu├Я auf dem Gyatrilied beruht, oder da├Я der Tristubhfu├Я aus dem Tristubhlied herausgebildet wurde, oder da├Я der Jagatfu├Я auf dem Jagatlied beruht.

+Grassmann

Wie an die G─Бjatr─л-Zeile die G─Бjatr─л-Zeile gef├╝gt wird, wie aus der Trischtubh-Zeile die [neue] Trischtubh-Zeile entspringt, oder wie die Dschagat─л-Zeile an die Dschagat─л-Zeile gef├╝gt wird, welche das verstehen, die haben Unsterblichkeit erlangt.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe constructs the prayer with the g─Бyatr─л metre; with the prayer (he constructs) the Soma, and with the triс╣гс╣нubh metre the couplet (or triplet); with the couplet (or triplet) he constructs the hymn with (verses of) two or four distichs; and with the syllable they construct the seven metres.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

G─Бyatreс╣Зa parimim─лte arkam: he, severally measures the mantra with the g─Бyatr─л metre;or, a part being put for the whole, with any Vedic metre; tс╣Ыс╣гс╣нubhena v─Бkam: v─Бka signifies either dvс╣Ыca or tс╣Ыca r┼лpam, the form or phrase of two or three hymns; or, it may imply a s┼лkta; v─Бkena v─Бkam: the first v─Бka is interpreted as s┼лkta, when repeated it implies the varga or anuv─Бka; if v─Бka signifies a couplet or triplet, is may be applicable to the s┼лkta; akс╣гarena sapta v─Бс╣З─лс╕е = the seven genitive ric metres of the Veda with the syllable, the syllable being the chief element of the metre; g─Бyatr─л has eight syllables; trс╣гс╣нubh has eleven syllables; jagat─л has twelve syllables. The classification of the metrical system of the Vedas is ascribed to Brahm─Б or the с╣Ыс╣гis, the priests

+Jamison Brereton

By the g─Бyatr─л (track) [=line] one measures the chant; by the chant the melody; by the triс╣гс╣нubh (track) [=line] (one measures) the
recitation;
by the two-footed and the four-footed recitation the (full) recitation. By the syllable the seven voices assume their measure.

+Griffith

With Gayatri he measures out the praise-song, Sama with praise-song, triplet with the Tristup.
The triplet with the two or four-foot measure, and with the syllable they form seven metres.

+Geldner

Nach dem Gyatrifu├Я bildet er die Gesangesstrophe, nach der Gesangesstrophe die Sangesweise, nach dem Tristubhfu├Я die Sprechstrophe, nach der zweif├╝├Яigen, der vierf├╝├Яigen Sprechstrophe das vorgetragene Lied. Mit der Silbe bilden sie die sieben Stimmen.

+Grassmann

Nach dem Versmass der G─Бjatr─л misst er das Preislied [ark├б], nach dem Preislied das Singlied [s├вman], nach dem Versmass der Trischtubh das Spruchlied [v─Бc├б], nach dem zweizeiligen und vierzeiligen Spruchmasse das Spruchlied, nach den Silben messen sie die sieben Versmasse.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬWith the hymns in the jagat─л metre he fixed the rain in heaven, and surveyed the Sun in the rathantara. They have declared three divisions of the g─Бyatr─л metre, whence it surpasses (all the rest) in force and majesty.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Fixed the rain in heaven: sindhum dvi astabh─Бyat: Brahm─Б, at the time of creation, fixed the sheder of water, udakasya syandakam, in the sky; or, a refernce is to ─Аditya: j─Бgato v─Б eс╣гa ya eс╣гa tapati: he may be termed j─Бgata who gives heat (to the world);

Rathantara: a portion of the S─Бma; Praj─Бpati beheld the sun in the hymn which sustains it: tad─Бdh─Бra bh┼лt─Бy─Бm с╣Ыci; g─Бyatra metre: g─Бyatrasya samidhas tisra ─Бhuс╕е: samidh signifies pada, a division of a hymn; of which g─Бyatr─л metre has three

+Jamison Brereton

By the jagat [=jagat─л] (stanza) he buttressed the river in heaven; in the rathantara (chant), he watched over the Sun.
They say that there are three kindling sticks [=three lines in a g─Бyatr─л stanza] belonging to the g─Бyatr─л (stanza). By its greatness it [=the
g─Бyatr─л stanza] has passed beyond those in greatness.

+Griffith

With Jagati the flood in heaven he stablished, and saw the Sun in the Rathantara Saman.
Gayatri hath, they say, three brands for kindling: hence it excels in majesty and vigour.

+Geldner

Mit der Jagatweise festigte er den Strom am Himmel, im Rathantara entdeckte er die Sonne. Sie sagen, da├Я das Gayatriversma├Я drei Brennh├╢lzer habe. Darum ├╝berragt es die anderen Metren an Macht und Gr├╢├Яe.

+Grassmann

Durch das Dschagat─л-Lied befestigte er den Strom am Himmel, in dem Rathantara-Liede erblickte er die Sonne; drei Flammen, sagt man, geh├╢ren dem Gajatr─л-Masse zu; darum ragte es durch seine Macht und Gr├╢sse hervor.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI invoke the cow that is easily milked, that the handy milker may milk her; may Savit─Б accept this our excellent libation, that his heat may (thereby) increase; it is for this, verily, that I earnestly invoke him.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The cow is the cloud, the milk is the rain; V─Бyu or win, is the milker; the metaphor is continued in the following three hymns, where the calf is the world or mankind anxious for the rain, as the cause of abundance

+Jamison Brereton

I summon this milk-cow giving good milk, and the deft-handed milker will milk her.
Savitar will impel the most excellent impetus in us. The gharma pot has been heated: this shall I proclaim.

+Griffith

I invocate the milch-cow good for milking so that the milker, deft of hand, may drain her.
May Savitar give goodliest stimulation. The caldron is made hot; I will proclaim it.

+Geldner

Ich locke diese gutmelkende Kuh heran und der Melker mit geschickter Hand soll sie melken. Die beste Weisung soll uns Savitri geben. Der Milchkessel steht am Feuer. Dies melde ich fein.

+Grassmann

Ich rufe herbei diese sch├╢nmilchende Kuh und der sch├╢nh├дndige Kuhmelker [der Priester] m├╢ge sie melken; die heilsamste Erquickung m├╢ge uns Savitar schaffen; der Kessel ist ans Feuer gesetzt, das will ich verk├╝nden.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson

тАЬShe comes lowing, abounding in rich (products), desiring her calf in her mind;may this cow grant her milk to the A┼Ыvins; may she thrive for our great advantage.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

Making the sound hiс╣Е, the goods-mistress of goods, seeking her calf, has come near through (my) thinking.
Let this inviolable cow give milk to the A┼Ыvins. Let her increase for our great good fortune.

+Griffith

She, lady of all treasure, is come hither yearning in spirit for her calf and lowing.
May this cow yield her milk for both the Asvins, and may she prosper to our high advantage.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe cow bellows for her calf, (who stands) with winking eyes, and lows as (she proceeds to lick his forehead; she utters a cry, as, anxious, she sees the moisture in the corners of his mouth, and nourishes him with her milk.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

The cow bellowed after her blinking calf. She made the sound hiс╣Е against his head (for him) to bellow.
Lowing toward his hot jaw, she bellows her bellow and swells her swell of milk.

+Griffith

The cow hath lowed after her blinking youngling; she licks his forehead, as she lows, to form it.
His mouth she fondly calls to her warm udder, and suckles him with milk while gently lowing.

+Geldner

Die Kuh bl├╢kte nach dem Kalb, das die Augen ├╢ffnet, seinen Kopf beschn├╝ffelte sie, um zu bl├╢ken. Nach dem hei├Яen Maule des Kalbes verlangend bl├╢kt sie ihr bl├╢ken. Sie strotzt von Milch.

+Grassmann

Die Kuh bl├╢kte hin nach dem schlummernden Kalbe, sie streckte den Kopf vor, um ihr ┬╗Hing┬л zu bl├╢ken; seinem warmen Maule entgegenbr├╝llend l├дsst sie ihr Gebl├╢k ert├╢nen, und tr├дnkt es mit ihrer Milch.

+Elizarenkova

тАЬHe, too, bellows, and the cow utters inarticulate sounds, as, encompassed by him, she repairs to her stall; (influenced) by her instrumental ncts, she acts like a human being, and, radiant, manifests her nature.тАЭ

This humsтАФthat by which the cow is enclosed. She bellows her bellow, resting upon the smoky (fire).

+Griffith

He also snorts, by whom encompassed round the Cow laws as she clings unto the shedder of the rain.
She with her shrilling cries hath humbled mortal man, and, turned to lightning, hath stripped off her covering robe.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬLife endowed with breath, eager (in discharge of its functions), reposes, steady, in the midst of its (proper) abodes; the life of the mortal body, cognate with the mortal frame, endures immortal (sustained) by (obsequial) offerings.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

By obsequial offerings: svadh─Бbhiс╕е putra kс╣Ыtaiс╕е, by offerings made by the sons

+Jamison Brereton

Breathing, life rests (though remaining) on its headlong course, stirring (though) steadfast in the midst of the dwelling places.
The living one keeps moving by the will of the dead one; the immortal one shares the same womb with the mortal one.

+Griffith

That which hath breath and speed and life and motion lies firmly stablished in the midst of houses.
Living, by offerings to the Dead he moveth Immortal One, the brother of the mortal.

+Geldner

Atmend ruht das Leben und ist doch schnellen Ganges, sich regend und doch fest inmitten der Fl├╝sse. Die Seele des Toten wandert nach eigenem Ermessen. Die unsterbliche Seele ist gleichen Ursprungs mit dem Sterblichen.

+Grassmann

Das athmende, das rasch gehende, das lebendige, das sich regende, das feste liegt in der Mitte der Wohnsitze; der Lebendige wandert mit der Kraft des Verstorbenen (?); der Unsterbliche ist gleichen Schoosses mit dem Sterblichen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI have beheld the unwearied protector of the universe, the sun, travelling upwards, the downwards by various paths;invested with aggregative and diffusive radiance, he revolves in the midst of the regions.тАЭ

+Jamison Brereton

I saw the herdsman who never settles down, roaming here and afar along his paths.
Clothing himself in those that converge and diverge, he moves back and forth among living beings.

+Griffith

I saw the Herdsman, him who never stumbles, approaching by his pathways and departing.
He, clothed with gathered and diffusive splendour, within the worlds continually travels.

+Geldner

Ich sah den Hirten auf seinen Wegen hin und her gehen ohne zu rasten. Er h├╝llte sich in die Gew├дsser, die in gleicher und in entgegengesetzter Richtung laufen und bewegt sich hin und her in den Gesch├╢pfen.

+Grassmann

Ich sah den H├╝ter, welcher nimmer hinf├дllt, der hin und her auf seinen Pfaden wandert; sich h├╝llend in die gleichen und verschiednen [Strahlen], geht hin und her er innerhalb der Welten. [= 1003, 3]

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬHe who has made (this state of things) does not comprehend it; he who has beheld it, has it also verily hidden (from him); he, whilst yet enveloped in his mother’s womb, is subject to many births, and has entered upon evil.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

He who has: Man; Nirukta, considers wind as the cause of rain and alludes to it allegorically

+Jamison Brereton

He who created him does not know him. He is far away from him who has seen him.
He is surrounded within the womb of his mother. Having many
offspring, he has entered into destruction.

+Griffith

He who hath made him cloth not comprehend him: from him who saw him surely is he hidden.
He, yet enveloped in his Mother’s bosom, source of much life, hath sunk into destruction.

+Geldner

Wer ihn hervorgebracht hat, der kennt ihn nicht; wer ihn gesehen hat, dem entschwindet er. In den Scho├Я der Mutter eingeh├╝llt ist er der Vernichtung verfallen, w├дhrend er viele Nachkommen hat.

+Grassmann

Der ihn geschaffen hat, der kennt ihn nicht; der ihn gesehen hat, vor dem ist er verborgen; wenn er noch vom Mutterschose umh├╝llt ist, ist er, der kinderreiche [die Regeng├╝sse als Kinder des Blitzes gedacht], schon dem Untergang verfallen.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe heaven is my parent and progenitor; the navel (of the earth) is my kinsman; the spacious earth is my mother. The womb (of all beings) lies between the two uplifted ladles, and in it the parent has deposited the germ (of the fruitfulness) of the daughter.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

My parent: n─Бbhir atra bandhu: n─Бbhi is related to me pit─Б janit─Б, i.e. the moisture of the earth, by which corn is abundant, and which, as derived from the rain of heaven, makes the latter the parent and progenitor of man;

Bandhuс╕е = bandhik─Б, binding or supporting; this word is an epithet of pс╣Ыthiv─л, the earth; two uplifted ladles: utt─Бnayos’ camvor yonir antar: the uplifted ladles are heaven and earth, and the womb of all beings between them is the firmament, the region of the rain; the parent has deposited: the father, the heaven, may be regarded as identical with either ─Аditya or Indra; the daughter is the earth, whose fertility depends upon the rain deposited as a germ in the firmament

+Jamison Brereton

[The Sun:] тАЬMy father, my progenitor, is Heaven; here is my navel. My mother, this great Earth, is my relation.
My womb is within the two open cups [=Heaven and Earth]. Here my father placed the child [=the Sun] of his daughter [=Dawn].тАЭ

+Griffith

Dyaus is my Father, my begetter: kinship is here. This great earth is my kin and Mother.
Between the wide-spread world-halves is the birth-place: the Father laid the Daughter’s germ within it.

+Geldner

Der Himmel ist mein Vater, der Erzeuger, dort ist mein Nabel. Diese gro├Яe Erde ist meine Sippe, die Mutter. In diesen hat der Vater die Leibesfrucht der Tochter gelegt.

+Grassmann

┬╗Der Himmel ist mein Vater und Erzeuger, dort ist mein Ursprung, meine Mutter und Verwandte ist diese weite Erde; zwischen den beiden weit ausgedehnten Weltschalen ist der Schooss [der mich getragen hat], dorthin setzte der Vater die Leibesfrucht der Tochter.┬л

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI ask you, (instrumental tutor of the rite), what is the uttermost end of the earth; I ask you, where is the navel of the world. I ask you, what is the fecundating power of the rain-shedding steed; I ask you, what is the supreme heaven of (holy) speech.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The next hymn answers the questions

+Jamison Brereton

I ask you about the farthest end of the earth. I ask where is the navel of the living world.
I ask you about the seed of the bull(-like) horse. I ask about the highest heaven of speech.

+Griffith

I ask thee of the earth’s extremest limit, where is the centre of the world, I ask thee.
I ask thee of the Stallion’s seed prolific, I ask of highest heaven where Speech abideth.

+Geldner

Ich frage dich nach der ├дu├Яersten Grenze der Erde, ich frage dich wo der Nabel der Welt ist? Ich frage dich nach dem Samen des Hengstes, ich frage dich nach dem h├╢chsten Inbegriff der Rede.

+Grassmann

Ich frage dich nach dem ├дussersten Ende der Erde, ich frage, wo der Welt Nabel ist; ich frage dich nach dem Samen des besamenden Hengstes, ich frage nach dem h├╢chsten Himmel, wo die Rede [v├вc] thront.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThis altar is the uttermost end of the earth; this sacrifice is the navel of the world; this Soma is the fecundating power of the rain-shedding steed; this Brahm─Б is the supreme heavn of (holy) speech.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

This altar: et─Бvat─л vai pс╣Ыthiv─л y─Бv─Бt─л vediс╕е, such or so much, verily, as the earth, so much is the altar; it is the essence of the whole earth (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 2.6.4); the navel of the world: n─Бbhi = sannahana, the binding together of man with the mans of subsistence, or the crops that spring from the rain which falls as the consequence of sacrifice or of oblations; holy speech: the texts of the Vedas, of which Brahm─Б, or the priest, is the author ir expounder

+Jamison Brereton

This altar here is the farthest end of the earth. This sacrifice here is the navel of the living world.
This soma here is the seed of the bull(-like) horse. This formulator here is the highest heaven of speech.

+Griffith

This altar is the earth’s extremest limit; this sacrifice of ours is the world’s centre.
The Stallion’s seed prolific is the Soma; this Brahman highest heaven where Speech abideth.

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe seven (sustaining), the embryo (rain) for half a year, the fecundating (element) of the world, abide, by appointment, in the various functions of Viс╣гс╣Зu. By their intelligence they pervade in thought all around (them), for they are intelligent and diffusive.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The seven: the solar rays, sapt─Бrdhagarbh─Бс╕е; either retaining the rains for half a year, i.e. during the dry months, or abiding in a part or half of space, or in the mid-heaven or firmament. Viс╣гс╣Зu is the pervading sun; vy─Бpakasya ─Аdityasya, in whose various duties of cherishing the world, the solar rays are, by direction, pradi┼Ы─Б, especially employed

+Jamison Brereton

The seven children of the (two world-)halves [=the Seven Seers], the seed of the living world, take their place by the direction of Viс╣гс╣Зu in the spreading expanse.
By their insights and their thought these encompassing perceivers of inspired words encompass (everything) everywhere.

+Griffith

Seven germs unripened yet are heaven’s prolific seed: their functions they maintain by Visnu’s ordinance.
Endued with wisdom through intelligence and thought, they compass us about present on every side.

+Geldner

Sieben Halbs├╢hne sind besch├дftigt, nach Vishnu┬┤s Weisung den Samen der Welt zu verteilen. Sie ├╝berragen an Gedanken und Verstand allenthalben, diese ├╝berragenden Weisen.

+Grassmann

Sieben aus einer Welth├дlfte [der Erde] geborene stehen als der Welt Samen auf Geheiss des Vischnu am Himmel [es scheinen die sieben с╣Щс╣гi gemeint, welche als die sieben Sterne des grossen B├дren an den Himmel versetzt sind], sie, die durch Gedanken und Geist weisen, sie, die umfangenden umfangen sch├╝tzend das All.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬI distinguish not if I am this all; for I go perplexed, and bound in mind; when the first-born (perceptions) of the truth reach me, then immediately shall I obtain a portion (of the meaning) of that (sacred) word.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

I distinguish not: na vij─Бn─Бmi yadiva idam asmi: this may be read as: yadi va idam, that I am like that which this is; or, if I am this; in either meaning, the philosophical implication is the identity of individual and universal spirit

+Jamison Brereton

I do not understand what sort of thing I am here: though bound, I roam about in secret by my thinking.
When the first-born of truth [=Agni] has come to me, only then do I attain a share of this speech here.

+Griffith

What thing I truly am I know not clearly: mysterious, fettered in my mind I wander.
When the first-born of holy Law approached me, then of this speech I first obtain a portion.

+Geldner

Ich verstehe nicht, was dem vergleichbar ist, was ich bin. Ich wandele, heimlich mit dem Denken ausger├╝stet. Sobald der Erstgeborene der Weltordnung ├╝ber mich gekommen ist, da erlange ich Anteil an dieser Rede.

+Grassmann

Ich weiss nicht, was ich eben bin; innerlich ger├╝stet im Geiste wandere ich; als zu mir kam der erst geborene des heiligen Werkes, da erst erlangte ich den Antheil dieser heiligen Rede.

+Elizarenkova

+Wilson
English translation:

тАЬThe immortal cognate with the mortal, affected by (desire of) enjoyment, goes to the lower or the upper (sphere); but (men beholding them) associated, going everywhere (in this world together); going everywhere (in other worlds together); have comprehended the one, but have not comprehended the other.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Affected by desire or enjoyment: svadhy─Б gс╣Ыbh─лtaс╕е = liс╣н, seized by food; i.e., any sensual gratification; have comprehended the one: they have not distinguished between body and soul; or, they have not made any distinction between the three kinds of bodies with which soul is invested, the gross body, the subtle body, and the union of the two

+Jamison Brereton

He goes inward and outward, controlled by his own willтАФhe, the immortal one of the same womb as the mortal one.
Those two are ever going apart in different directions. They observe the one; they do not observe the other.

+Griffith

Back, forward goes he, grasped by strength inherent, the Immortal born the brother of the mortal
Ceaseless they move in opposite directions: men mark the one, and fail to mark the other.

+Geldner

R├╝ckw├дrts, vorw├дrts geht er durch Eigengesetz festgehalten. Der Unsterbliche ist gleichen Ursprungs mit dem Sterblichen. Diese beiden gehen best├дndig nach verschiedener Richtung auseinander. Wenn man den einen wahrnimmt, nimmt man den anderen nicht wahr.

+Grassmann

Es schreitet r├╝ckw├дrts und vorw├дrts der aus eigner Lust ergriffene Unsterbliche [der Gott, der den S├дnger begeistert], der mit dem Sterblichen [S├дnger] gleichen Ursprung hat; sie beide gehen fort und fort nach verschiedenen Seiten, den einen sieht man [den S├дnger], den andern [den Gott] sieht man nicht.

+Elizarenkova
